[2] Day 1: The Island
[3] 1
[4] "Although it's an old cliché," said Ellery, a tall and handsome young man, "to me, the detective novel is an intellectual game, a stimulating logical game between the reader and the detective, or between the reader and the author, and nothing more. Therefore, the so-called 'socialist realism' that is popular in Japan is vulgar and unbearable. The detective who finally catches the lover and boss after enduring hardships after the death of a single woman living in a bachelor apartment – I hate this kind of plot. Bribery, corruption, political scandals, and tragedies caused by the distorted modern society – I can't stand it either. The suitable themes for detective novels, even if criticized for being outdated, are still the detective, the large mansion, the strange inhabitants, the bloody tragedies, the impossible crimes, and the shocking plots... Although absurd, it doesn't matter, the most important thing is to find the fun in that world. Of course, it's the fun of an intellectual game, right?
[5] Surrounded by an endless sea, these people were sitting on a fishing boat emitting the smell of gasoline and rumbling forward.
[6] "It's so annoying," said Carl, scowling as he sat on the boat's railing. He tilted his chin, which was pale and pointed upwards, "I don't like it when you keep talking about 'intellectuality,' Ellery. You can define detective novels as a game, but don't bring up intellectuality so casually. It sounds awkward to me."
[7] "I didn't expect you to say that."
[8] "This is what you call the psychology of voters. Not all readers are like you, Ellery."
[9] "That's true," Ellery said solemnly, looking straight at the other person. "I've always felt regret about it. I've deeply felt it when walking around campus. Just take our research group, for example, not everyone is intellectual, and there are also people like the South Gate in there."
[10] "Do you want to argue?"
[11] "Of course not." Ellery shrugged, "No one is targeting you. And what I mean by 'intellectualism' is the attitude towards the game, not the cleverness or stupidity of a person. There is no one in the world who does not have intellectuality, and there is no one who does not know the game. What I want to say is whether or not one has the corresponding spirit to play the game intellectually."
[12] "Hmph." Carl snorted and turned his head to the side.
[13] Ellery looked at the short, young man standing beside him, wearing round glasses and a youthful face, and smiled gently.
[14] "Leroux, if deduction is understood as a world that exists for intellectual games based on its unique methodology, then deduction will have difficulty standing in our modern society."
[15] "Ah." Leroux tilted his head, not understanding.
[16] "This is an old topic. Working tirelessly, strong organizational skills, the most advanced forensic science search techniques... Today's police are not ordinary people, but rather, they are so capable that it can be troublesome. The problem lies in the fact that the famous detectives of old, who relied solely on their gray brain cells as weapons, no longer have room to show off their talents in modern society. If Sherlock appeared in today's society, he would probably be known for his comedic antics rather than his detective skills."
[17] "That's an exaggeration. There must be modern Sherlock Holmes in modern society."
[18] "Yes, of course. Perhaps he would appear with the most advanced forensic medicine and identification knowledge, and would spend half an hour explaining it to the pitiful Watson, listing a bunch of obscure technical terms and formulas that readers would never understand. It's clear as day, Watson; don't you understand this, Watson..."
[19] Ellery slipped his hands into the pockets of his yellowish-gray double-breasted overcoat and lightly shrugged his shoulders.
[20] "I gave an extreme example earlier, but what I want to convey is exactly this. I don't believe in the victory of the uninspiring police force - the detective search techniques they use surpass the elegant 'theories' and 'deductions' that golden-age detectives took for granted. For writers who write detective novels set in modern society, the most efficient way to solve this dilemma, albeit an inappropriately chosen word, is the 'murder mansion' scenario I mentioned earlier."
[21] "I see." Leroux nodded solemnly. "So the most modern theme of the classic detective story is 'And Then There Were None', right?"
[22] At the end of March, despite the approaching spring, the sea breeze still brought a chill.
[23] From the S Peninsula on the east coast of Kyushu, Japan, a ship set sail from the small port of S District, J Cape, heading towards a small island floating five kilometers away from the sea.
[24] It was a good day for sailing, but the place was inevitably accompanied by sand in spring, so the sky was more gray-white. The shimmering sea surface was bathed in yellow sunlight, and the yellow sand blown from the distant continent enveloped everything in a thin mist, making everything hazy.
[25] "I don't see any other ships."
[26] A tall boy put his hand on the other side of the ship's railing. His name was Edgar Allan Poe, who had been smoking silently, and his messy hair looked listless, and his full beard was unkempt.
[27] "The wind is rough on the other side of the island, and all the ships have gone around," said the elderly fisherman. "The fishing grounds are further south, and there are few ships that go to that island after leaving port – you guys are really different students."
[28] "Is that so?"
[29] "Your names are strange, calling yourself 'Leroux' and 'Elliott', all strange. Do you have the same name?"
[30] "Yes, that's our alias."
[31] "So, all college students call each other by such names now?"
[32] "No, that's not the case."
[33] "Well, you are quite the unique students then."
[34] Two girls sat on a long wooden box in the center of the boat, along with the fisherman's son steering at the back. There were eight people on the boat in total.
[35] The six other people on the boat, excluding the fisherman and his son, were all students from K\*\* University in O City, Biga Prefecture, and members of the university's mystery research club. "Elliott", "Carl", "Leru" - as Elliot Poe had mentioned, these were the nicknames they used among themselves.
[36] It is clear that these nicknames are derived from the American mystery writers they idolize, Ellery Queen, John Dixon Carr, Gaston Leroux, and Edgar Allan Poe. The two girls are named "Agatha" and "Ochizu," respectively named after the Queen of Mystery Agatha Christie and Baroness Ochizu, known for her novel "The Old Man in the Corner."
[37] "Look over there! We can see the houses on the island of Kuro."
[38] The fisherman shouted out loud, and the six young people turned their gaze towards the small island that was getting closer.
[39] A flat island.
[40] A nearly vertical rock wall rose from the sea, covered in a lush green, resembling a stack of giant ten-yen coins. Three corners protruded forward, perhaps the origin of the island's name.
[41] Surrounded by steep cliffs, the island had only a narrow bay where small fishing boats could barely dock. As a result, only fishing enthusiasts occasionally visited this forgotten island. Twenty years ago, someone built a unique house named "Blue House" on the island and moved in, but now it is a deserted island.
[42] "Is it the place where the cliff sticks out?" Agatha stood up and asked loudly. She excitedly narrowed her eyes and looked forward, while pressing down her wavy hair that was blowing in the wind.
[43] "Yes. That's the only remaining annex. I heard the main house was burned down completely."
[44] "Hmm. Is that 'Tenjoukan'?" Ellery asked the fisherman. "Have you ever been to the island?"
[45] "I've come to the bay to take shelter several times, but I've never gone up. Especially after that incident, I've never come close to this place again. Be careful."
[46] "Careful about what?" Agatha turned around and asked.
[47] The fisherman lowered his voice. "It's said that the island is haunted."
[48] Agatha and Osiz were startled and exchanged glances.
[49] "There are ghosts, the man who was killed, named Nakamura."
[50] The fisherman's wrinkled black face broke into a sinister smile. "I heard it from others, that when it rains and you pass by the island, you can see a white figure on the cliff waving at you; it's Nakamura's ghost, inviting people. It's also said that the uninhabited annex is lit up, and there are ghosts wandering around the ruins; fishing boats that go to the island to fish are overturned in the sea by ghosts."
[51] "It doesn't matter, old man," Ellery politely interrupted him. "It doesn't matter. You tell us these scary stories, and we'll be even happier."
[52] In fact, out of the six young people, only Ozzy, sitting on the wooden box, seemed a little timid. Agatha was unfazed and even excitedly shouted, "Great, great!" and ran to the stern, shouting loudly at the young son of the captain steering the boat, "Is it true?"
[53] "It's all nonsense," the boy glanced at Agatha and quickly averted his eyes, answering stiffly, "I've heard it from others, but I haven't seen it with my own eyes."
[54] "Oh, is that so?" Agatha's face showed a hint of dissatisfaction, but soon she laughed mischievously again. "But having ghosts isn't a bad thing either, after all, it's the crime scene."
[55] March 26, 1986, Tuesday, just after 11 a.m.

On both sides are steep cliffs, with the precipitous rock on the right side facing the cliffs extending to the south shore of the island, forming a cliff about twenty meters high. On the east coast, the cliff is even higher, reaching fifty meters.

[80] The seventh person to join the group for the next seven days in this house - Van - made his appearance. Needless to say, the name is inspired by the creator of the famous detective Philo Vance, S.S. Van Dine.
[81] "Just a moment, I'll be right out." Fan said in a hoarse voice, then closed the shutter door and ran out.

[86] A grand procession of people, led by Fung, entered the Jiyu-guan.
[87] After entering the blue door, they found themselves in a spacious foyer - it seemed spacious, but it quickly became apparent that this was an illusion, as the room was not rectangular and therefore appeared larger than it actually was.
[88] At the end of the wall, there was another pair of double doors leading to the interior. Upon closer inspection, the wall was narrower than the one facing the entrance, which meant that the foyer was a trapezoidal plane that gradually narrowed from the outside in.
[89] The six people other than Fung found the design that caused sensory illusions to be quite perplexing. After passing through the door leading to the interior and entering the central hall of the house, they discovered that the room was an equilateral ten-sided polygon, and they finally understood.
[90] To grasp the structure of the Jiyu-guan, it is best to visualize a simple floor plan in your mind.
[91] The ten-sided hall, as the name suggests, has a ten-sided exterior shape - a regular ten-sided polygon. Inside this large ten-sided polygon is a smaller ten-sided polygon, the central hall. Two vertices connected by a straight line form ten rooms. In other words, the central hall of the ten-sided polygon is surrounded by ten rooms with equilateral trapezoidal shapes, one of which is the entrance hall they just passed through.
[92] "How do you like it?" Fan turned around and said to everyone, "The door opposite the entrance leads to the kitchen, the left side is the bathroom and toilet, and the remaining seven rooms are guest rooms."
[93] "Ten-sided houses and a ten-sided central hall," Ellery looked around and walked to the large table in the center of the room, tapping the corner of the white table with his finger, "The table is also ten-sided. Is it possible that the deceased Nakamura Seisuke was an obsessive?"
[94] "Perhaps," Leroux replied, "It is said that the main building, Blue House, which was burnt down, had everything from the floor to the ceiling to the furniture painted blue."
[95] Twenty years ago, the person who built Blue House and moved to the island was Nakamura Seisuke. Of course, the person who built the annex, the ten-sided hall, was also Nakamura Seisuke.
[96] "But –" Agatha murmured, "Won't we get lost in the rooms?"
[97] The relative central hall and kitchen have white wooden double doors with patterned glass, and it's difficult to distinguish them when closed. The doors to the rooms arranged on both sides of the four walls are also made of white wood and are equally indistinguishable. Without any distinctive objects to differentiate them, it's no wonder Agatha had doubts.
[98] "Yes, I almost went into the wrong room several times this morning," Rang said with a wry smile, his eyes a bit swollen from the fever, "We could put nameplates on the doors – Osizu, did you bring the sketchbook?"
[99] Suddenly called by name, Osizu quickly raised her head.
[100] She was a petite girl who always wore dark clothes to conceal her slightly plump figure, making her look dull. In contrast to the lively Agatha, she had a submissive demeanor, but she was skilled in drawing Japanese paintings.

[103] "OK, understood," Agatha replied cheerfully, "Let's rest for a while and then explore the island."

[108] The walls were painted white, and the floor was covered with large blue tiles, so you could walk in without taking off your shoes. In the center of the hall was an octagonal skylight, and sunlight streamed through it, illuminating the octagonal table in white. There were ten white chairs with blue covers around the table, and the only decoration in the room was a light bulb hanging from the ceiling.
[109] The island was without power, and the only light in the room came from the natural light streaming through the skylight, giving the octagonal hall an indescribable air of mystery even in the daytime.

In the end, it was not found at the crime scene. This is the general situation of the case, Leroux?"

[750] Chapter 3
[751] The Second Day - The Island
[752] 1
[753] She woke up drowsily.
[754] Although she went to bed at two o'clock in the morning after returning to her room, she couldn't fall asleep for a long time. She lay awake in the darkness, her mind troubled by the unpleasant events of the day that refused to leave her.
[755] Ellery, Van, Allan Poe, Agatha, Leroux, and Carr - she did not dislike these six people, on the contrary, she had a certain degree of goodwill towards all members - including Van - of the group. What she disliked was herself for living with them.
[756] In her everyday life, no matter what troubles she faced, she could always find solace when she returned to her residence. Once inside her house, it was her personal world where she could let her imagination run wild and immerse herself in it. There were her best friends, the perfect lover, and passionate admirers. She could become the alluring woman she desired.
[757] However -
